- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls

# Compliance Evidence Bundle: SSO Settings Feature in Grafana

## Scenario

For a SOC 2 audit, your security team needs a compliance evidence bundle proving
that Grafana's SSO (Single Sign-On) settings control is implemented end-to-end.
You need to trace the `ssoSettingsApi` feature flag from its definition through
the SSO settings infrastructure, API endpoints, OAuth connector wiring, and
authentication registration to show the control is properly gated and enforced.

## Your Task

Find ALL files in `grafana/grafana` that form the SSO settings control across
these 4 layers:

### 1. Feature Flag Definition
- The feature flag registry where `ssoSettingsApi` is defined
- Generated constants files (Go, TypeScript) that reference this flag

### 2. SSO Settings Infrastructure
- The `Service` interface definition for SSO settings management
- The `Reloadable` interface for live configuration reloading
- The `SSOSettings` data model/struct with persistence annotations
- The `SSOSettingsStore` database layer for SSO setting persistence

### 3. API & Authentication Wiring
- The REST API endpoint registration (`/api/v1/sso-settings`) with access control middleware
- The `SocialService` provider that loads OAuth connectors when the flag is enabled
- The authentication client registration that conditionally enables LDAP based on the flag

### 4. Access Control & DI Registration
- The access control evaluators (`EvalAuthenticationSettings`, `OauthSettingsEvaluator`) that gate SSO admin UI access
- The `ProvideService` dependency injection function that wires the SSO settings store, API, fallback strategies, and reloadables

## Available Resources

Your ecosystem includes the following repositories:
- `grafana/grafana` at v11.4.0
- `grafana/loki` at v3.3.4

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "grafana/grafana", "path": "pkg/services/featuremgmt/registry.go"}
  ],
  "text": "Comprehensive explanation of how the 4 layers connect: feature flag definition → SSO settings infrastructure → API & authentication wiring → access control & DI registration."
}
```

**Important**: Use `grafana/grafana` as the exact `repo` identifier. Strip the
`github.com/` prefix that Sourcegraph MCP tools return.

**Deep Search hint**: This task requires synthesizing across feature management,
SSO settings infrastructure, OAuth connectors, and authentication registration
layers. Deep Search is particularly well-suited for tracing these cross-cutting
concerns.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find the architecturally significant files across all 4 layers?
- **Keyword coverage**: Does your answer reference the key interfaces and types (`ssoSettingsApi`, `FlagSsoSettingsApi`, `SSOSettings`, `Reloadable`, `SSOSettingsStore`)?
- **Provenance**: Does your answer cite the correct repos and directory paths?
- **Rubric judge**: An LLM judge will assess evidence completeness, cross-component tracing, auditor actionability, and technical accuracy.

## Summary

**Answer file created: `/workspace/answer.json`**

The comprehensive tracing reveals how the SSO settings control is architecturally implemented:

### **Layer 1: Feature Flag Definition**
- **registry.go** (lines 934-941): Master definition with stage, owner, and configuration
- **toggles_gen.go** (line 508): Auto-generated Go constant `FlagSsoSettingsApi`

### **Layer 2: SSO Settings Infrastructure**
- **ssosettings.go**: Three critical interfaces:
  - `Service`: CRUD operations + reload capabilities  
  - `Reloadable`: Live configuration reloading interface
  - `Store`: Database persistence abstraction
- **models.go**: `SSOSettings` struct with Xorm ORM mapping to `sso_setting` table
- **database.go**: `SSOSettingsStore` implementing database operations

### **Layer 3: API & Authentication Wiring**
- **api/api.go** (lines 30-76): `/api/v1/sso-settings` endpoints with access control middleware
- **ssosettingsimpl/service.go** (lines 47-100): **Critical gate** - API only registered when feature flag enabled
- **socialimpl/service.go** (lines 40-111): **Conditional OAuth loading** - loads connectors from database when flag enabled, falls back to config files when disabled

### **Layer 4: Access Control & DI Registration**
- **ssoutils/utils.go**: `EvalAuthenticationSettings()` and `OauthSettingsEvaluator()` for permission gating
- **authn/authnimpl/registration.go** (lines 55-61): **Conditional LDAP registration** - registers LDAP client only when `FlagSsoSettingsApi && FlagSsoSettingsLDAP` or traditional config enabled

The architecture demonstrates a **centralized feature gate** that controls API availability, OAuth connector loading,

**pkg/services/ssosettings/ssosettings.go** and consists of three critical interfaces:\\n\\n1. **Service Interface** (lines 15-37): Core business logic for managing SSO settings with methods:\\n   - `List()` / `ListWithRedactedSecrets()`: Retrieve all SSO settings\\n   - `GetForProvider()` / `GetForProviderWithRedactedSecrets()`: Fetch provider-specific settings\\n   - `Upsert()` / `Delete()` / `Patch()`: Create/update/delete operations\\n   - `RegisterReloadable()` / `Reload()`: Live configuration reloading\\n\\n2. **Reloadable Interface** (lines 39-45): Allows providers to:\\n   - `Reload()`: Apply configuration changes at runtime\\n   - `Validate()`: Validate and compare SSO settings before persisting\\n\\n3. **Store Interface** (lines 56-64): Database abstraction for SSO settings persistence:\\n   - `Get()`, `List()`, `Upsert()`, `Delete()` operations\\n\\nThe **SSOSettings Model** (pkg/services/ssosettings/models/models.go, lines 46-59) defines the data structure:\\n- Xorm ORM annotations map to `sso_setting` table\\n- JSON marshaling converts between snake_case (database) and camelCase (API)\\n- Tracks source (database vs system/config file) for audit and administration\\n\\nThe **SSOSettingsStore Implementation** (pkg/services/ssosettings/database/database.go, lines 20-32) wraps the SQL store and implements the Store interface for database persistence.\\n\\n## Layer 3: API & Authentication Wiring\\n\\n### REST API Endpoint Registration\\n\\n**pkg/services/ssosettings/api/api.go** (lines 30-76) defines the `Api` struct with dependency injection:\\n\\n```go\\nfunc ProvideApi(\\n  ssoSettingsSvc ssosettings.Service,\\n  routeRegister routing.RouteRegister,\\n  ac ac.AccessControl,\\n) *Api\\n```\\n\\nEndpoints are registered at `/api/v1/sso-settings` (line 63) with access control middleware:\\n- `GET /`: List all SSO settings (ActionSettingsRead)\\n- `GET /:key`: Get provider settings (ActionSettingsRead + OAuthScopeSettings)\\n- `PUT /:key`: Update settings (ActionSettingsWrite + OAuthScopeSettings)\\n- `DELETE /:key`: Remove settings (ActionSettingsWrite + OAuthScopeSettings)\\n\\n### Service Provider Registration\\n\\n**pkg/services/ssosettings/ssosettingsimpl/service.go** (lines 47-100) contains the critical `ProvideService()` function which:\\n\\n1. **Conditionally Enables the API** (lines 94-96):\\n   ```go\\n   if features.IsEnabledGlobally(featuremgmt.FlagSsoSettingsApi) {\\n     ssoSettingsApi := api.ProvideApi(svc, routeRegister, ac)\\n     ssoSettingsApi.RegisterAPIEndpoints()\\n Conditionally adds LDAP to available providers\\n   - FlagSsoSettingsSAML: Conditionally adds SAML to available providers\\n   - AllOAuthProviders: Base list of OAuth providers (GitHub, GitLab, Google, etc.)\\n\\n3. **Wires Fallback Strategies** (lines 51-54):\\n   - NewOAuthStrategy: Load OAuth settings from config files/env\\n   - NewLDAPStrategy: Load LDAP settings from config files/env\\n   - NewSAMLStrategy: Load SAML settings (enterprise feature)\\n\\n### Social Service (OAuth Connector) Wiring\\n\\n**pkg/login/social/socialimpl/service.go** (lines 40-111) demonstrates the feature flag gating:\\n\\n```go\\nif features.IsEnabledGlobally(featuremgmt.FlagSsoSettingsApi) {\\n  allSettings, err := ssoSettings.List(context.Background())\\n  // Load OAuth connectors from SSO settings database (lines 57-81)\\n} else {\\n  // Fallback: Load OAuth connectors from config files (lines 82-106)\\n}\\n```\\n\\nWhen `FlagSsoSettingsApi` is enabled:\\n- OAuth connectors are loaded dynamically from the database (`ssoSettings.List()`)\\n- Connectors are created from SSOSettings via `CreateOAuthConnector()`\\n- Settings source can be database, config files, or environment variables\\n\\nWhen disabled:\\n- OAuth configuration falls back to traditional ini-style config files\\n- Config is read from `[auth.provider_name]` sections\\n\\n## Layer 4: Access Control & Authentication Client Registration\\n\\n### Access Control Evaluators\\n\\n**pkg/services/accesscontrol/ssoutils/utils.go** (lines 8-24) defines the evaluators:\\n\\n1. **EvalAuthenticationSettings()** (lines 8-15): Gates access to SAML and LDAP admin UI:\\n   - Requires ActionSettingsWrite OR ActionSettingsRead on ScopeSettingsSAML\\n   - OR ActionLDAPStatusRead\\n\\n2. **OauthSettingsEvaluator()** (lines 17-24): Gates OAuth settings access:\\n   - Dynamically evaluates ActionSettingsRead and ActionSettingsWrite\\n   - For each configurable OAuth provider from `cfg.SSOSettingsConfigurableProviders`\\n   - Returns EvalAny() allowing access if user can read OR write any OAuth provider\\n\\nThese evaluators are used in the API middleware (api.go, line 64) to enforce permissions per endpoint.\\n\\n### Authentication Client Registration\\n\\n**pkg/services/authn/authnimpl/registration.go** (lines 55-61) conditionally registers LDAP authentication:\\n\\n```go\\nssoSettingsLDAP := features.IsEnabledGlobally(featuremgmt.FlagSsoSettingsApi) && \\n                    features.IsEnabledGlobally(featuremgmt.FlagSsoSettingsLDAP)\\nif cfg.LDAPAuthEnabled || ssoSettingsLDAP {\\n  ldap := clients.ProvideLDAP(cfg, ldapService, userService, authInfoService)\\n  proxyClients = append(proxyClients, ldap)\\n  passwordClients = append(passwordClients, ldap)\\n}\\n```\\n\\nThis enables LDAP authentication client when:\\n- Traditional LDAP config is enabled (`cfg.LDAPAuthEnabled`), OR\\n- Both FlagSsoSettingsApi AND FlagSsoSettingsLDAP feature flags are enabled\\n\\nThe OAuth client registration (lines 98-101) registers OAuth clients dynamically from `socialService.GetOAuthProviders()`, which is itself controlled by whether connectors were loaded from database (SSO settings) vs config files.\\n\\n## End-to-End Control Flow\\n\\n1. **Feature Flag Definition**: `FlagSsoSettingsApi` defined in registry.go, exported as constant in toggles_gen.go\\n\\n2. **Database Layer**: SSOSettings model with Xorm persistence to `sso_setting` table; Store interface abstracts database access\\n\\n3. **Service Layer**: ProvideService checks feature flag and conditionally:\\n   - Instantiates SSOSettingsStore for database operations\\n   - Registers SSOSettingsApi REST endpoint handler\\n   - Loads SSO settings from database and registers reloadables\\n   - Configures OAuth providers from database when flag enabled\\n\\n4. **API Layer**: /api/v1/sso-settings endpoints registered with access control middleware using EvalAuthenticationSettings and OauthSettingsEvaluator\\n\\n5. **Authentication Wiring**: \\n   - SocialService loads OAuth connectors from database (when flag enabled) or config (when disabled)\\n   - Registration layer conditionally registers LDAP and OAuth authentication clients based on feature flags and loaded providers\\n\\n## Compliance Audit Trail\\n\\nFor SOC 2 evidence, this architecture demonstrates:\\n\\n- **Centralized Control**: Single feature flag gates entire SSO settings subsystem\\n- **Enforcement Points**: \\n  - API endpoint registration (service.go:94-96)\\n  - Connector loading (socialimpl/service.go:56)\\n  - LDAP client registration (registration.go:56-61)\\n- **Access Control**: Mandatory permission checks via AccessControl middleware on all /api/v1/sso-settings endpoints\\n- **Audit Capability**: SSOSettings model tracks Created/Updated timestamps and source (DB vs config file)\\n- **Fallback Behavior**: When feature flag disabled, system gracefully falls back to config file-based configuration (no disruption)\\n\"\n}\n",
